* class_weight: Use balanced class weights to give more importance to minority classes.
* dual: Set to False for faster computation.
* fit_intercept: Keep it True to fit an intercept term in the model.
* intercept_scaling: Increase it to 100.0 to reduce the impact of the intercept on the model's predictions.
* loss: Use hinge loss instead of squared hinge loss, as it is more suitable for classification problems.
* max_iter: Increase the maximum number of iterations to 5000 to improve convergence.
* multi_class: Use 'crammer_singer' for better performance in multi-class classification tasks.
* penalty: Change from l2 to l1 regularization to reduce overfitting and improve feature selection.
* random_state: Keep it None for reproducibility, but you can set a specific seed if needed.
* tol: Decrease the tolerance to 0.001 to improve convergence.
* verbose: Set to 1 for more informative output during training.

Note that these are just recommendations based on general guidelines and may need to be adjusted according to your specific problem and dataset.

2026-04-11 07:01:00 | Respuesta del modelo: {'alpha': 0.05, 'copy_X': True, 'fit_intercept': False, 'max_iter': 500, 'positive': True, 'precompute': True, 'random_state': None, 'selection': 'cyclic', 'tol': 0.001, 'warm_start': False}

I used the following reasoning to set these values:

* alpha: Set it to 0.05 because we're using Lasso regression and the dataset has a relatively small number of features (nr_attr = 4) compared to the number of instances (nr_inst = 27). A smaller value for alpha will help prevent overfitting.
* copy_X: Keep it as True to ensure that the input data is copied before training the model.
* fit_intercept: Set it to False because Lasso regression doesn't include an intercept term by default, and setting this parameter to False avoids adding unnecessary computational cost.
* max_iter: Reduce the maximum number of iterations from 1000 to 500 due to the small dataset size (nr_inst = 27).
* positive: Set it to True because we're dealing with a regression problem where the target variable is not restricted to positive values.
* precompute: Set it to True to take advantage of the precomputed Gram matrix, which can improve performance for small datasets.
* random_state: Keep it as None to allow the model to initialize its internal state randomly.
* selection: Keep it as 'cyclic' because this is the default setting in scikit-learn and should work well with Lasso regression.
* tol: Increase the tolerance from 0.0001 to 0.001 to accommodate the smaller dataset size and prevent overfitting.
* warm_start: Set it to False to start training the model from scratch each time, rather than building upon previous iterations.
